I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed/repo. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
ACIR != Brillig: `pop_back` returns wrong result in Brillig
### Aim

Discovered testing https://github.com/noir-lang/noir/pull/9262

The following program fails in ACIR but returns a wrong result in Brillig:

```rust
global G_A: [Field] = &[-282608142060723387702497189224219065418];
fn main() -> pub Field {
    let (a, _) = G_A.pop_back();
    let (_, f) = a.pop_back();
    f
}
```

### Expected Behavior

They should both fail because the slice has only 1 item, so we can't pop twice.

### Bug

```console
❯ cargo run -q -p nargo_cli -- execute --force-brillig
[fuzz_testing] Circuit witness successfully solved
[fuzz_testing] Witness saved to target/fuzz_testing.gz
[fuzz_testing] Circuit output: Field(-282608142060723387702497189224219065418)

❯ cargo run -q -p nargo_cli -- execute --force
error: Index out of bounds, array has size 1, but index was -1
  ┌─ src/main.nr:4:18
  │
4 │     let (_, f) = a.pop_back();
  │                  ----------
  │
  = Call stack:
    1. src/main.nr:4:18

Failed to solve program: 'Index out of bounds, array has size 1, but index was -1'
```

RUST_LOG=debug NOIR_AST_FUZZER_SEED=0xe367188a00100000 cargo test -p noir_ast_fuzzer_fuzz pass_vs_prev

     1	use acvm::{AcirField, acir::brillig::MemoryAddress};
     2	
     3	use super::ProcedureId;
     4	use crate::brillig::brillig_ir::{
     5	    BrilligBinaryOp, BrilligContext,
     6	    brillig_variable::{BrilligVector, SingleAddrVariable},
     7	    debug_show::DebugToString,
     8	    registers::{RegisterAllocator, ScratchSpace},
     9	};
    10	
    11	impl<F: AcirField + DebugToString, Registers: RegisterAllocator> BrilligContext<F, Registers> {
    12	    /// Copy arguments to [ScratchSpace] and call [ProcedureId::VectorPopBack].
    13	    ///
    14	    /// Pops `item_pop_count` items from the back of a `source_vector`, returning the new `destination_vector`
    15	    /// and the pointer to the popped items in `read_pointer`.
    16	    ///
    17	    /// The `item_pop_count` equals the number of variables to pop into in SSA.
    18	    /// The `source_len` is the semantic (not flattened) length of the vector.
    19	    pub(crate) fn call_vector_pop_back_procedure(
    20	        &mut self,
    21	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    22	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    23	        destination_vector: BrilligVector,
    24	        read_pointer: MemoryAddress,
    25	        item_pop_count: usize,
    26	    ) {
    27	        let [
    28	            source_vector_length_arg,
    29	            source_vector_pointer_arg,
    30	            item_pop_count_arg,
    31	            destination_vector_pointer_return,
    32	            read_pointer_return,
    33	        ] = self.make_scratch_registers();
    34	
    35	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_length_arg, source_len.address);
    36	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_pointer_arg, source_vector.pointer);
    37	        self.usize_const_instruction(item_pop_count_arg, item_pop_count.into());
    38	
    39	        self.add_procedure_call_instruction(ProcedureId::VectorPopBack);
    40	
    41	        self.mov_instruction(destination_vector.pointer, destination_vector_pointer_return);
    42	        self.mov_instruction(read_pointer, read_pointer_return);
    43	    }
    44	}
    45	
    46	/// Compile [ProcedureId::VectorPopBack].
    47	pub(super) fn compile_vector_pop_back_procedure<F: AcirField + DebugToString>(
    48	    brillig_context: &mut BrilligContext<F, ScratchSpace>,
    49	) {
    50	    let [
    51	        source_vector_length_arg,
    52	        source_vector_pointer_arg,
    53	        item_pop_count_arg,
    54	        destination_vector_pointer_return,
    55	        read_pointer_return,
    56	    ] = brillig_context.allocate_scratch_registers();
    57	
    58	    let source_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: source_vector_pointer_arg };
    59	    let target_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: destination_vector_pointer_return };
    60	
    61	    // First we need to allocate the target vector decrementing the size by `item_pop_count`.
    62	    // We use the semantic length, rather than load the vector size from the meta-data,
    63	    // because after merging vectors of different lengths, the semantic length can be different
    64	    // then the number of items in the vector, which is the longer of the merged values.
    65	    let source_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    66	    brillig_context.codegen_vector_flattened_size(
    67	        source_size.address,
    68	        source_vector_length_arg,
    69	        item_pop_count_arg,
    70	    );
    71	
    72	    // We will pop a number of (flattened) items; targets_size = source_size - item_pop_count
    73	    let target_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    74	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
    75	        source_size.address,
    76	        item_pop_count_arg,
    77	        target_size.address,
    78	        BrilligBinaryOp::Sub,
    79	    );
    80	
    81	    let rc = brillig_context.codegen_read_vector_rc(source_vector);
    82	
    83	    let is_rc_one = brillig_context.codegen_usize_equals_one(*rc);
    84	
    85	    let source_vector_items_pointer =
    86	        brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(source_vector);
    87	
    88	    brillig_context.codegen_branch(is_rc_one.address, |brillig_context, is_rc_one| {
    89	        if is_rc_one {
    90	            // We can reuse the source vector, updating its length
    91	            brillig_context.mov_instruction(target_vector.pointer, source_vector.pointer);
    92	            brillig_context.codegen_update_vector_size(target_vector, *target_size);
    93	        } else {
    94	            // We need to clone the source vector; allocate memory for it.
    95	            brillig_context.codegen_initialize_vector(target_vector, *target_size, None);
    96	
    97	            let target_vector_items_pointer =
    98	                brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(target_vector);
    99	
   100	            // Now we copy the source vector starting at index 0 into the target vector but with the reduced length.
   101	            brillig_context.codegen_mem_copy(
   102	                *source_vector_items_pointer,
   103	                *target_vector_items_pointer,
   104	                *target_size,
   105	            );
   106	
   107	            // We don't decrease the RC of the source vector, otherwise repeatedly popping the same item
   108	            // from the original (immutable) handle would bring its RC down to 1.
   109	        }
   110	    });
   111	
   112	    // Finally set the pointer where the popped items can be read from to the source vector.
   113	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
   114	        *source_vector_items_pointer,
   115	        target_size.address,
   116	        read_pointer_return,
   117	        BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
   118	    );
   119	}

     1	//! Codegen for converting SSA slice intrinsic functions to Brillig bytecode.
     2	use acvm::acir::brillig::MemoryAddress;
     3	
     4	use crate::brillig::brillig_ir::{
     5	    BrilligBinaryOp,
     6	    brillig_variable::{BrilligVariable, BrilligVector, SingleAddrVariable},
     7	    registers::RegisterAllocator,
     8	};
     9	
    10	use super::super::brillig_block::BrilligBlock;
    11	
    12	impl<Registers: RegisterAllocator> BrilligBlock<'_, Registers> {
    13	    /// Take a list of [BrilligVariable] and copy the memory they point at to the `write_pointer`,
    14	    /// increasing the address by 1 between each variable.
    15	    fn write_variables(&mut self, write_pointer: MemoryAddress, variables: &[BrilligVariable]) {
    16	        for (index, variable) in variables.iter().enumerate() {
    17	            self.brillig_context.store_instruction(write_pointer, variable.extract_register());
    18	            if index != variables.len() - 1 {
    19	                self.brillig_context.codegen_usize_op_in_place(
    20	                    write_pointer,
    21	                    BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
    22	                    1,
    23	                );
    24	            }
    25	        }
    26	    }
    27	
    28	    /// Prepare a vector for pushing a number of new (flattened) items to the back,
    29	    /// then write those variables to the returned write pointer.
    30	    pub(crate) fn slice_push_back_operation(
    31	        &mut self,
    32	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
    33	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    34	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    35	        variables_to_insert: &[BrilligVariable],
    36	    ) {
    37	        let write_pointer = self.brillig_context.allocate_register();
    38	        self.brillig_context.call_prepare_vector_push_procedure(
    39	            source_len,
    40	            source_vector,
    41	            target_vector,
    42	            *write_pointer,
    43	            variables_to_insert.len(),
    44	            true,
    45	        );
    46	
    47	        self.write_variables(*write_pointer, variables_to_insert);
    48	    }
    49	
    50	    /// Prepare a vector for pushing a number of new (flattened) items to the front,
    51	    /// then write those variables to the returned write pointer.
    52	    pub(crate) fn slice_push_front_operation(
    53	        &mut self,
    54	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
    55	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    56	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    57	        variables_to_insert: &[BrilligVariable],
    58	    ) {
    59	        let write_pointer = self.brillig_context.allocate_register();
    60	        self.brillig_context.call_prepare_vector_push_procedure(
    61	            source_len,
    62	            source_vector,
    63	            target_vector,
    64	            *write_pointer,
    65	            variables_to_insert.len(),
    66	            false,
    67	        );
    68	
    69	        self.write_variables(*write_pointer, variables_to_insert);
    70	    }
    71	
    72	    /// Read the memory starting at the pointer into successive variables.
    73	    fn read_variables(&mut self, read_pointer: MemoryAddress, variables: &[BrilligVariable]) {
    74	        for (index, variable) in variables.iter().enumerate() {
    75	            self.brillig_context.load_instruction(variable.extract_register(), read_pointer);
    76	            if index != variables.len() - 1 {
    77	                self.brillig_context.codegen_usize_op_in_place(
    78	                    read_pointer,
    79	                    BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
    80	                    1,
    81	                );
    82	            }
    83	        }
    84	    }
    85	
    86	    /// Read the popped number of variables from the front of the source vector,
    87	    /// then create the target vector from the source by skipping the number of popped items.
    88	    pub(crate) fn slice_pop_front_operation(
    89	        &mut self,
    90	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
    91	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    92	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    93	        removed_items: &[BrilligVariable],
    94	    ) {
    95	        let read_pointer = self.brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(source_vector);
    96	        self.read_variables(*read_pointer, removed_items);
    97	
    98	        self.brillig_context.call_vector_pop_front_procedure(
    99	            source_len,
   100	            source_vector,
   101	            target_vector,
   102	            removed_items.len(),
   103	        );
   104	    }
   105	
   106	    /// Create new vector with a number of (flattened) items popped from the back,
   107	    /// then read the popped items into the variables representing the removed items.
   108	    pub(crate) fn slice_pop_back_operation(
   109	        &mut self,
   110	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
   111	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
   112	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
   113	        removed_items: &[BrilligVariable],
   114	    ) {
   115	        let read_pointer = self.brillig_context.allocate_register();
   116	        self.brillig_context.call_vector_pop_back_procedure(
   117	            source_len,
   118	            source_vector,
   119	            target_vector,
   120	            *read_pointer,
   121	            removed_items.len(),
   122	        );
   123	
   124	        self.read_variables(*read_pointer, removed_items);
   125	    }
   126	
   127	    /// Prepare a vector for inserting a number of (flattened) items at a specific index
   128	    /// by making a hole for them, then write the variables to the returned write pointer.
   129	    pub(crate) fn slice_insert_operation(
   130	        &mut self,
   131	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
   132	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
   133	        index: SingleAddrVariable,
   134	        items: &[BrilligVariable],
   135	    ) {
   136	        let write_pointer = self.brillig_context.allocate_register();
   137	
   138	        self.brillig_context.call_prepare_vector_insert_procedure(
   139	            source_vector,
   140	            target_vector,
   141	            index,
   142	            *write_pointer,
   143	            items.len(),
   144	        );
   145	
   146	        self.write_variables(*write_pointer, items);
   147	    }
   148	
   149	    /// Read a number of (flattened) items at a specific index of a vector into the variables
   150	    /// representing the removed items, then create a new vector with the same number of
   151	    /// items removed and subsequent items shifted to the left.
   152	    pub(crate) fn slice_remove_operation(
   153	        &mut self,
   154	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
   155	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
   156	        index: SingleAddrVariable,
   157	        removed_items: &[BrilligVariable],
   158	    ) {
   159	        let read_pointer = self.brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(source_vector);
   160	        self.brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
   161	            *read_pointer,
   162	            index.address,
   163	            *read_pointer,
   164	            BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
   165	        );
   166	        self.read_variables(*read_pointer, removed_items);
   167	
   168	        self.brillig_context.call_vector_remove_procedure(
   169	            source_vector,
   170	            target_vector,
   171	            index,
   172	            removed_items.len(),
   173	        );
   174	    }
   175	}

   202	    fn create_test_environment() -> (Ssa, FunctionContext, BrilligContext<FieldElement, Stack>) {
   203	        let mut builder = FunctionBuilder::new("main".to_string(), Id::test_new(0));
   204	        builder.set_runtime(RuntimeType::Brillig(InlineType::default()));
   205	        builder.terminate_with_return(vec![]);
   206	        let ssa = builder.finish();
   207	        let mut brillig_context = create_context(ssa.main_id);
   208	        brillig_context.enter_context(Label::block(ssa.main_id, Id::test_new(0)));
   209	
   210	        let function_context = FunctionContext::new(ssa.main(), true);
   211	        (ssa, function_context, brillig_context)
   212	    }
   213	
   214	    fn create_brillig_block<'a>(
   215	        function_context: &'a mut FunctionContext,
   216	        brillig_context: &'a mut BrilligContext<FieldElement, Stack>,
   217	        globals: &'a HashMap<ValueId, BrilligVariable>,
   218	        hoisted_global_constants: &'a HashMap<(FieldElement, NumericType), BrilligVariable>,
   219	    ) -> BrilligBlock<'a, Stack> {
   220	        let variables = BlockVariables::default();
   221	        BrilligBlock {
   222	            function_context,
   223	            block_id: Id::test_new(0),
   224	            brillig_context,
   225	            variables,
   226	            last_uses: Default::default(),
   227	            globals,
   228	            hoisted_global_constants,
   229	            building_globals: false,
   230	        }
   231	    }

   233	    #[test]
   234	    fn test_slice_push_operation() {
   235	        fn test_case_push(
   236	            push_back: bool,
   237	            source_len: usize,
   238	            source: Vec<FieldElement>,
   239	            item_to_push: FieldElement,
   240	            expected_return: Vec<FieldElement>,
   241	        ) {
   242	            // Types of arguments passed to the entry point.
   243	            let arguments = vec![
   244	                // The input size semantic length.
   245	                BrilligParameter::SingleAddr(BRILLIG_MEMORY_ADDRESSING_BIT_SIZE),
   246	                // The input slice of the array items, with a known size/capacity.
   247	                BrilligParameter::Slice(
   248	                    vec![BrilligParameter::SingleAddr(BRILLIG_MEMORY_ADDRESSING_BIT_SIZE)],
   249	                    source.len(),
   250	                ),
   251	                // The item to push.
   252	                BrilligParameter::SingleAddr(BRILLIG_MEMORY_ADDRESSING_BIT_SIZE),
   253	            ];
   254	            // We expect 1 item to be pushed. The capacity might be more, depending on reuse.
   255	            let result_length = source_len + 1;
   256	            assert_eq!(
   257	                result_length,
   258	                expected_return.len(),
   259	                "expected return data should be 1 longer than the input"
   260	            );
   261	            // Returned data expected to be leading with length and capacity, followed by the items.
   262	            let result_length_with_metadata = result_length + 2;
   263	
   264	            // Entry points don't support returning slices, so we implicitly cast the vector to an array
   265	            // With the metadata at the start.
   266	            let returns = vec![BrilligParameter::Array(
   267	                vec![BrilligParameter::SingleAddr(BRILLIG_MEMORY_ADDRESSING_BIT_SIZE)],
   268	                result_length_with_metadata,
   269	            )];
   270	
   271	            let (_, mut function_context, mut context) = create_test_environment();
   272	
   273	            // Allocate the parameters
   274	            let source_len_var = context.allocate_single_addr_mem();
   275	            let source_vector = context.allocate_brillig_vector();
   276	            let item_to_insert = context.allocate_single_addr_mem();
   277	
   278	            // Allocate the results
   279	            let target_vector = context.allocate_brillig_vector();
   280	
   281	            let brillig_globals = HashMap::default();
   282	            let hoisted_globals = HashMap::default();
   283	            let mut block = create_brillig_block(
   284	                &mut function_context,
   285	                &mut context,
   286	                &brillig_globals,
   287	                &hoisted_globals,
   288	            );
   289	
   290	            if push_back {
   291	                block.slice_push_back_operation(
   292	                    *target_vector,
   293	                    *source_len_var,
   294	                    *source_vector,
   295	                    &[item_to_insert.to_var()],
   296	                );
   297	            } else {
   298	                block.slice_push_front_operation(
   299	                    *target_vector,
   300	                    *source_len_var,
   301	                    *source_vector,
   302	                    &[item_to_insert.to_var()],
   303	                );
   304	            }
   305	
   306	            context.codegen_return(&[target_vector.to_var()]);
   307	
   308	            // Compile to byte code.
   309	            let bytecode = create_entry_point_bytecode(context, arguments, returns).byte_code;
   310	
   311	            // Prepare flattened inputs.
   312	            let inputs = [vec![source_len.into()], source, vec![item_to_push]].concat();
   313	
   314	            // Execute the byte code.
   315	            let (vm, return_data_offset, return_data_size) = create_and_run_vm(inputs, &bytecode);
   316	
   317	            assert_eq!(
   318	                return_data_size, result_length_with_metadata,
   319	                "expect result length to be data+meta"
   320	            );
   321	
   322	            let mut returned_vector: Vec<FieldElement> = vm.get_memory()
   323	                [return_data_offset..(return_data_offset + result_length_with_metadata)]
   324	                .iter()
   325	                .map(|mem_val| mem_val.to_field())
   326	                .collect();
   327	
   328	            let returned_size = returned_vector.remove(0);
   329	            assert_eq!(returned_size, result_length.into(), "expect size to be input+1");
   330	
   331	            let _returned_capacity = returned_vector.remove(0);
   332	            assert_eq!(
   333	                returned_vector, expected_return,
   334	                "expect items after size and capacity to be input+new"
   335	            );
   336	        }
   337	
   338	        test_case_push(
   339	            true,
   340	            3,
   341	            vec![
   342	                FieldElement::from(1_usize),
   343	                FieldElement::from(2_usize),
   344	                FieldElement::from(3_usize),
   345	            ],

    11	    /// Pushes one or more elements to the back of a non-nested slice.
    12	    ///
    13	    /// # Arguments
    14	    ///
    15	    /// * `arguments[0]` - Current slice length
    16	    /// * `arguments[1]` - Slice contents
    17	    /// * `arguments[2..]` - Elements to push back
    18	    /// * `result_ids[0]` - Updated slice length
    19	    /// * `result_ids[1]` - Update slice contents
    20	    ///
    21	    /// # Returns
    22	    ///
    23	    /// A vector of [AcirValue]s containing:
    24	    /// 1. Updated slice length (incremented by one)
    25	    /// 2. New slice with elements appended
    26	    pub(super) fn convert_slice_push_back(
    27	        &mut self,
    28	        arguments: &[ValueId],
    29	        dfg: &DataFlowGraph,
    30	        result_ids: &[ValueId],
    31	    ) -> Result<Vec<AcirValue>, RuntimeError> {
    32	        let slice_length = self.convert_value(arguments[0], dfg).into_var()?;
    33	        let slice_contents = arguments[1];
    34	        let elements_to_push = &arguments[2..];
    35	
    36	        // Increase the slice length by one to enable accessing more elements in the slice.
    37	        let one = self.acir_context.add_constant(FieldElement::one());
    38	
    39	        let slice = self.convert_value(slice_contents, dfg);
    40	        let slice_typ = dfg.type_of_value(slice_contents);
    41	
    42	        let new_slice_val = if let Some(len_const) = dfg.get_numeric_constant(arguments[0]) {
    43	            // Length is known at compile time - we can precisely determine where to write
    44	            let mut new_slice = self.read_array_with_type(slice, &slice_typ)?;
    45	            // length of Acir Values slice
    46	            let len = len_const.to_u128() as usize * elements_to_push.len();
    47	            for (i, elem) in elements_to_push.iter().enumerate() {
    48	                let element = self.convert_value(*elem, dfg);
    49	                let write_index = len + i;
    50	
    51	                // If the array is already large enough, replace the element at the write position.
    52	                // Otherwise, append to the end.
    53	                if write_index < new_slice.len() {
    54	                    new_slice[write_index] = element;
    55	                } else {
    56	                    new_slice.push_back(element);
    57	                }
    58	            }
    59	            AcirValue::Array(new_slice)
    60	        } else {
    61	            // Length is not known, we are going to:
    62	            // 1. Push dummy data to the slice, so that it's capacity covers for the push_back
    63	            // 2. Generate a DynamicArray corresponding to the new slice flattened content
    64	            // 3. Write the elements to push to this array at the correct length
    65	            let value_types = flat_element_types(&slice_typ);
    66	            let Type::Slice(slice_types) = &slice_typ else {
    67	                unreachable!("ICE: slice operation on a non slice type");
    68	            };
    69	
    70	            let mut elements_var = Vec::new();
    71	            let mut element_size = 0;
    72	            let mut new_slice = self.read_array_with_type(slice.clone(), &slice_typ)?;
    73	            let zero = self.acir_context.add_constant(FieldElement::zero());
    74	
    75	            // 1. Convert the elements-to-push into flattened acir_var and at the same time
    76	            // push_back corresponding dummy zero values to the AcirValues slice.
    77	            for (elem, ssa_typ) in elements_to_push.iter().zip(slice_types.to_vec()) {
    78	                let element = self.convert_value(*elem, dfg);
    79	                element_size += super::arrays::flattened_value_size(&element);
    80	                match element {
    81	                    AcirValue::Var(acir_var, acir_type) => {
    82	                        new_slice.push_back(AcirValue::Var(zero, acir_type));
    83	                        elements_var.push(acir_var);
    84	                    }
    85	                    AcirValue::Array(vector) => {
    86	                        let zero_value = self.array_zero_value(&ssa_typ)?;
    87	                        new_slice.push_back(zero_value);
    88	                        for acir_value in vector {
    89	                            let acir_vars = self.flatten(&acir_value)?;
    90	                            elements_var.extend(acir_vars);
    91	                        }
    92	                    }
    93	                    AcirValue::DynamicArray(_) => {
    94	                        unimplemented!("pushing a dynamic array into a slice is not yet supported");
    95	                    }
    96	                }
    97	            }
    98	
    99	            // The actual flattened size of new_slice after the dummy push_back
   100	            let new_slice_array = AcirValue::Array(new_slice);
   101	            let len = super::arrays::flattened_value_size(&new_slice_array);
   102	
   103	            // 2. Copy the slice into an AcirDynamicArray
   104	            // Generates the element_type_sizes array
   105	            let element_type_sizes =
   106	                if super::arrays::array_has_constant_element_size(&slice_typ).is_none() {
   107	                    Some(self.init_element_type_sizes_array(
   108	                        &slice_typ,
   109	                        slice_contents,
   110	                        Some(&new_slice_array),
   111	                        dfg,
   112	                    )?)
   113	                } else {
   114	                    None
   115	                };
   116	
   117	            // The block ID for the new slice is the one for the resulting slice
   118	            let block_id = self.block_id(result_ids[1]);
   119	            self.initialize_array(block_id, len, Some(new_slice_array))?;
   120	            let flattened_dynamic_array =
   121	                AcirDynamicArray { block_id, len, value_types, element_type_sizes };
   122	
   123	            // 3. Write to the dynamic array
   124	
   125	            // 3.1 Computes the flatten_idx where to write into the dynamic array:
   126	            // Use element_type_size if it exists; convert the user index (slice_length) into the AcirValues index,
   127	            // and then flatten it with element_type_size
   128	            let mut flatten_idx = if let Some(element_type_sizes) = element_type_sizes {
   129	                let predicate_index = self
   130	                    .acir_context
   131	                    .mul_var(slice_length, self.current_side_effects_enabled_var)?;
   132	                let acir_element_size = self.acir_context.add_constant(elements_to_push.len());
   133	                let acir_value_index =
   134	                    self.acir_context.mul_var(predicate_index, acir_element_size)?;
   135	                self.acir_context
   136	                    .read_from_memory(element_type_sizes, &acir_value_index)
   137	                    .map_err(RuntimeError::from)?
   138	            } else {
   139	                // If it does not exist; the array is homogenous and we can simply multiply by size of the array elements
   140	                let element_size_var = self.acir_context.add_constant(element_size);
   141	                self.acir_context.mul_var(slice_length, element_size_var)?
   142	            };
   143	            // Write the elements to the dynamic array
   144	            for element in &elements_var {
   145	                self.acir_context.write_to_memory(block_id, &flatten_idx, element)?;
   146	                flatten_idx = self.acir_context.add_var(flatten_idx, one)?;
   147	            }
   148	            AcirValue::DynamicArray(flattened_dynamic_array)
   149	        };
   150	
   151	        let new_slice_length = self.acir_context.add_var(slice_length, one)?;
   152	        Ok(vec![AcirValue::Var(new_slice_length, NumericType::length_type()), new_slice_val])
   153	    }
   154	
   155	    /// Pushes one or more elements to the front of a non-nested slice.
   156	    ///
   157	    /// # Arguments
   158	    ///
   159	    /// * `arguments[0]` - Current slice length
   160	    /// * `arguments[1]` - Slice contents
   161	    /// * `arguments[2..]` - Elements to push to the front
   162	    ///
   163	    /// # Returns
   164	    ///
   165	    /// A vector of [AcirValue]s containing:
   166	    /// 1. Updated slice length (incremented by one)
   167	    /// 2. New slice with elements prepended
   168	    pub(super) fn convert_slice_push_front(
   169	        &mut self,
   170	        arguments: &[ValueId],
   171	        dfg: &DataFlowGraph,
   172	    ) -> Result<Vec<AcirValue>, RuntimeError> {
   173	        let slice_length = self.convert_value(arguments[0], dfg).into_var()?;
   174	        let slice_contents = arguments[1];
   175	        let elements_to_push = &arguments[2..];
   176	
   177	        // Increase the slice length by one to enable accessing more elements in the slice.
   178	        let one = self.acir_context.add_constant(FieldElement::one());
   179	        let new_slice_length = self.acir_context.add_var(slice_length, one)?;
   180	
   181	        let slice = self.convert_value(slice_contents, dfg);
   182	        let slice_type = dfg.type_of_value(slice_contents);
   183	        let mut new_slice = self.read_array_with_type(slice, &slice_type)?;
   184	
   185	        // We must directly push front elements for non-nested slices
   186	        for elem in elements_to_push.iter().rev() {
   187	            let element = self.convert_value(*elem, dfg);
   188	            new_slice.push_front(element);
   189	        }
   190	
   191	        let new_slice_val = AcirValue::Array(new_slice);
   192	
   193	        Ok(vec![AcirValue::Var(new_slice_length, NumericType::length_type()), new_slice_val])
   194	    }
   195	
   196	    /// Removes and returns one or more elements from the back of a non-nested slice.
   197	    ///
   198	    /// # Arguments
   199	    ///
   200	    /// * `arguments[0]` - Current slice length
   201	    /// * `arguments[1]` - Slice contents
   202	    /// * `result_ids[0]` - Updated slice length
   203	    /// * `result_ids[1]` - Update slice contents
   204	    /// * `result_ids[2..]` - Locations where popped elements will be stored
   205	    ///
   206	    /// # Returns
   207	    ///
   208	    /// A vector of [AcirValue]s containing:
   209	    /// 1. Updated slice length (decremented by one)
   210	    /// 2. Updated slice contents with the back elements removed
   211	    /// 3. Popped elements in order
   212	    ///
   213	    /// # Design
   214	    ///
   215	    /// The slice is represented in **flattened form** in memory. Popping the back
   216	    /// involves:
   217	    ///
   218	    /// 1. Decrementing the slice length by one.
   219	    /// 2. Using the decremented length as an offset for the elements to remove.
   220	    /// 3. Read out the elements located at that offset.
   221	    ///
   222	    /// The `result_ids` provided by the SSA to fetch the appropriate type information to be popped.
   223	    /// The `result_ids` encode the type/shape of the removed element.
   224	    ///
   225	    /// # Empty Slice Handling
   226	    ///
   227	    /// If the slice has zero length, this function skips the memory read and returns zero values.
   228	    /// It asserts that the current side effects must be disabled (predicate = 0), otherwise fails
   229	    /// with "cannot pop from a slice with length 0". This prevents reading from empty memory blocks
   230	    /// which would cause "Index out of bounds" errors.
   231	    pub(super) fn convert_slice_pop_back(
   232	        &mut self,
   233	        arguments: &[ValueId],
   234	        dfg: &DataFlowGraph,
   235	        result_ids: &[ValueId],
   236	    ) -> Result<Vec<AcirValue>, RuntimeError> {
   237	        let slice_length_var = arguments[0];
   238	        let slice_contents = arguments[1];
   239	
   240	        let slice_value = self.convert_value(slice_length_var, dfg);
   241	        let slice_length = slice_value.clone().into_var()?;
   242	        let block_id = self.ensure_array_is_initialized(slice_contents, dfg)?;
   243	        let slice = self.convert_value(slice_contents, dfg);
   244	
   245	        if self.has_zero_length(slice_contents, dfg) {
   246	            // Make sure this code is disabled, or fail with "Index out of bounds".
   247	            let msg = "cannot pop from a slice with length 0".to_string();
   248	            self.acir_context.assert_zero_var(self.current_side_effects_enabled_var, msg)?;
   249	
   250	            // Fill the result with default values.
   251	            let mut results = Vec::with_capacity(result_ids.len());
   252	
   253	            // The results shall be: [new len, new slice, ...popped]
   254	            results.push(slice_value);
   255	            results.push(slice);
   256	
   257	            for result_id in &result_ids[2..] {
   258	                let result_type = dfg.type_of_value(*result_id);
   259	                let result_zero = self.array_zero_value(&result_type)?;
   260	                results.push(result_zero);
   261	            }
   262	
   263	            return Ok(results);
   264	        }
   265	
   266	        // For unknown length under a side effect variable, we want to multiply with the side effect variable
   267	        // to ensure we don't end up trying to look up an item at index -1, when the semantic length is 0.
   268	        let is_unknown_length = dfg.get_numeric_constant(slice_length_var).is_none();
   269	
   270	        let one = self.acir_context.add_constant(FieldElement::one());
   271	        let mut new_slice_length = self.acir_context.sub_var(slice_length, one)?;
   272	
   273	        if is_unknown_length {
   274	            new_slice_length = self
   275	                .acir_context
   276	                .mul_var(new_slice_length, self.current_side_effects_enabled_var)?;
   277	        }
   278	
   279	        // For a pop back operation we want to fetch from the `length - 1` as this is the
   280	        // last valid index that can be accessed in a slice. After the pop back operation
   281	        // the elements stored at that index will no longer be able to be accessed.
   282	        let mut var_index = new_slice_length;
   283	
   284	        let slice_type = dfg.type_of_value(slice_contents);
   285	        let item_size = slice_type.element_types();
   286	        // Must read from the flattened last index of the slice in case the slice contains nested arrays.
   287	        let flat_item_size: u32 = item_size.iter().map(|typ| typ.flattened_size()).sum();
   288	        let item_size = self.acir_context.add_constant(flat_item_size);
   289	        var_index = self.acir_context.mul_var(var_index, item_size)?;
   290	
   291	        let mut popped_elements = Vec::new();
   292	        for res in &result_ids[2..] {
   293	            let elem = self.array_get_value(&dfg.type_of_value(*res), block_id, &mut var_index)?;
   294	            popped_elements.push(elem);
   295	        }
   296	
   297	        let mut new_slice = self.read_array_with_type(slice, &slice_type)?;
   298	        for _ in 0..popped_elements.len() {
   299	            new_slice.pop_back();
   300	        }
   301	
   302	        let mut results = vec![
   303	            AcirValue::Var(new_slice_length, NumericType::length_type()),
   304	            AcirValue::Array(new_slice),
   305	        ];
   306	        results.append(&mut popped_elements);
   307	
   308	        Ok(results)
   309	    }
   310	
   311	    /// Removes and returns one or more elements from the front of a non-nested slice.
   312	    ///
   313	    /// # Arguments
   314	    ///
   315	    /// * `arguments[0]` - Current slice length
   316	    /// * `arguments[1]` - Slice contents
   317	    /// * `result_ids[..element_size]` - Locations for the popped elements
   318	    /// * `result_ids[element_size]` - Updated slice length
   319	    /// * `result_ids[element_size + 1]` - Updated slice contents
   320	    ///
   321	    /// `element_size` refers to the result of [crate::ssa::ir::types::Type::element_size].
   322	    ///
   323	    /// # Returns
   324	    ///
   325	    /// A vector of [AcirValue]s containing:
   326	    /// 1. Popped elements in order
   327	    /// 2. Updated slice length (decremented by one)
   328	    /// 3. Updated slice contents with the front elements removed
   329	    ///
   330	    /// # Design
   331	    ///
   332	    /// Slices are stored in **flattened form** in memory. To pop from the front:
   333	    ///
   334	    /// 1. Decrement the slice length by the size of one element.
   335	    /// 2. Read out the first `element_size` values at index `0`.
   336	    /// 3. Shift the update slice's memory forward by `element_size` slots to represent the updated slice.
   337	    ///
   338	    /// Unlike in [Self::convert_slice_pop_back], the returned slice contents differ from the input:
   339	    /// the underlying array is logically truncated at the *front* rather than
   340	    /// the back. The `result_ids` ensure that this logical shift is applied
   341	    /// consistently with the element's type.
   342	    ///
   343	    /// # Empty Slice Handling
   344	    ///
   345	    /// If the slice has zero length, this function skips the memory read and returns zero values.
   346	    /// It asserts that the current side effects must be disabled (predicate = 0), otherwise fails
   347	    /// with "cannot pop from a slice with length 0". This prevents reading from empty memory blocks
   348	    /// which would cause "Index out of bounds" errors.
   349	    pub(super) fn convert_slice_pop_front(
   350	        &mut self,
   351	        arguments: &[ValueId],
   352	        dfg: &DataFlowGraph,
   353	        result_ids: &[ValueId],
   354	   <response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you. You should retry this tool after you have searched inside the file with `grep -n` in order to find the line numbers of what you are looking for.</NOTE>

  1086	    pub(super) fn has_zero_length(&mut self, array: ValueId, dfg: &DataFlowGraph) -> bool {
  1087	        if let Type::Array(_, size) = dfg.type_of_value(array) {
  1088	            size == 0
  1089	        } else {
  1090	            match &dfg[array] {
  1091	                Value::Instruction { .. } | Value::Param { .. } => {
  1092	                    let array_acir_value = self.convert_value(array, dfg);
  1093	                    match array_acir_value {
  1094	                        AcirValue::DynamicArray(AcirDynamicArray { len, .. }) => len == 0,
  1095	                        AcirValue::Array(values) => values.is_empty(),
  1096	                        AcirValue::Var(_, _) => {
  1097	                            unreachable!(
  1098	                                "ICE: Unexpected ACIR value for array or slice: {array_acir_value:?}"

    46	/// Compile [ProcedureId::VectorPopBack].
    47	pub(super) fn compile_vector_pop_back_procedure<F: AcirField + DebugToString>(
    48	    brillig_context: &mut BrilligContext<F, ScratchSpace>,
    49	) {
    50	    let [
    51	        source_vector_length_arg,
    52	        source_vector_pointer_arg,
    53	        item_pop_count_arg,
    54	        destination_vector_pointer_return,
    55	        read_pointer_return,
    56	    ] = brillig_context.allocate_scratch_registers();
    57	
    58	    let source_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: source_vector_pointer_arg };
    59	    let target_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: destination_vector_pointer_return };
    60	
    61	    // First we need to allocate the target vector decrementing the size by `item_pop_count`.
    62	    // We use the semantic length, rather than load the vector size from the meta-data,
    63	    // because after merging vectors of different lengths, the semantic length can be different
    64	    // then the number of items in the vector, which is the longer of the merged values.
    65	    let source_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    66	    brillig_context.codegen_vector_flattened_size(
    67	        source_size.address,
    68	        source_vector_length_arg,
    69	        item_pop_count_arg,
    70	    );
    71	
    72	    // We will pop a number of (flattened) items; targets_size = source_size - item_pop_count
    73	    let target_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    74	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
    75	        source_size.address,
    76	        item_pop_count_arg,
    77	        target_size.address,
    78	        BrilligBinaryOp::Sub,
    79	    );
    80	
    81	    let rc = brillig_context.codegen_read_vector_rc(source_vector);
    82	
    83	    let is_rc_one = brillig_context.codegen_usize_equals_one(*rc);
    84	
    85	    let source_vector_items_pointer =
    86	        brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(source_vector);
    87	
    88	    brillig_context.codegen_branch(is_rc_one.address, |brillig_context, is_rc_one| {
    89	        if is_rc_one {
    90	            // We can reuse the source vector, updating its length
    91	            brillig_context.mov_instruction(target_vector.pointer, source_vector.pointer);
    92	            brillig_context.codegen_update_vector_size(target_vector, *target_size);
    93	        } else {
    94	            // We need to clone the source vector; allocate memory for it.
    95	            brillig_context.codegen_initialize_vector(target_vector, *target_size, None);
    96	
    97	            let target_vector_items_pointer =
    98	                brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(target_vector);
    99	
   100	            // Now we copy the source vector starting at index 0 into the target vector but with the reduced length.
   101	            brillig_context.codegen_mem_copy(
   102	                *source_vector_items_pointer,
   103	                *target_vector_items_pointer,
   104	                *target_size,
   105	            );
   106	
   107	            // We don't decrease the RC of the source vector, otherwise repeatedly popping the same item
   108	            // from the original (immutable) handle would bring its RC down to 1.
   109	        }
   110	    });
   111	
   112	    // Finally set the pointer where the popped items can be read from to the source vector.
   113	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
   114	        *source_vector_items_pointer,
   115	        target_size.address,
   116	        read_pointer_return,
   117	        BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
   118	    );
   119	}

     2	
     3	use super::ProcedureId;
     4	use crate::brillig::brillig_ir::{
     5	    BrilligBinaryOp, BrilligContext,
     6	    brillig_variable::{BrilligVector, SingleAddrVariable},
     7	    codegen_memory::VectorMetaData,
     8	    debug_show::DebugToString,
     9	    registers::{RegisterAllocator, ScratchSpace},
    10	};
    11	
    12	impl<F: AcirField + DebugToString, Registers: RegisterAllocator> BrilligContext<F, Registers> {
    13	    /// Copy arguments to [ScratchSpace] and call [ProcedureId::VectorPopFront].
    14	    ///
    15	    /// Pops items from the front of a vector, returning the new vector.
    16	    /// The procedure assumes that there are constraints to prevent 0 size vectors from being popped.
    17	    pub(crate) fn call_vector_pop_front_procedure(
    18	        &mut self,
    19	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    20	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    21	        destination_vector: BrilligVector,
    22	        item_pop_count: usize,
    23	    ) {
    24	        let [
    25	            source_vector_length_arg,
    26	            source_vector_pointer_arg,
    27	            item_pop_count_arg,
    28	            destination_vector_pointer_return,
    29	        ] = self.make_scratch_registers();
    30	
    31	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_length_arg, source_len.address);
    32	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_pointer_arg, source_vector.pointer);
    33	        self.usize_const_instruction(item_pop_count_arg, item_pop_count.into());
    34	
    35	        self.add_procedure_call_instruction(ProcedureId::VectorPopFront);
    36	
    37	        self.mov_instruction(destination_vector.pointer, destination_vector_pointer_return);
    38	    }
    39	}
    40	
    41	/// Compile [ProcedureId::VectorPopFront].
    42	pub(super) fn compile_vector_pop_front_procedure<F: AcirField + DebugToString>(
    43	    brillig_context: &mut BrilligContext<F, ScratchSpace>,
    44	) {
    45	    let [
    46	        source_vector_length_arg,
    47	        source_vector_pointer_arg,
    48	        item_pop_count_arg,
    49	        destination_vector_pointer_return,
    50	    ] = brillig_context.allocate_scratch_registers();
    51	
    52	    let source_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: source_vector_pointer_arg };
    53	    let target_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: destination_vector_pointer_return };
    54	
    55	    let VectorMetaData {
    56	        rc: source_rc,
    57	        size: source_size,
    58	        capacity: source_capacity,
    59	        items_pointer: source_items_pointer,
    60	    } = brillig_context.codegen_read_vector_metadata(
    61	        source_vector,
    62	        Some((source_vector_length_arg, item_pop_count_arg)),
    63	    );
    64	
    65	    // target_size = source_size - item_pop_count
    66	    // Assumes constraints exist against underflow.
    67	    // We don't have to worry about the semantic length of merged vectors here, because we are popping from the front.
    68	    let target_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    69	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
    70	        source_size.address,
    71	        item_pop_count_arg,
    72	        target_size.address,
    73	        BrilligBinaryOp::Sub,
    74	    );
    75	
    76	    let is_rc_one = brillig_context.codegen_usize_equals_one(*source_rc);
    77	
    78	    brillig_context.codegen_branch(is_rc_one.address, |brillig_context, is_rc_one| {
    79	        if is_rc_one {
    80	            // We reuse the source vector, moving the metadata to the right (decreasing capacity)
    81	            // Set the target vector pointer to be the source plus the number of popped items.
    82	            brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
    83	                source_vector.pointer,
    84	                item_pop_count_arg,
    85	                target_vector.pointer,
    86	                BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
    87	            );
    88	            // Decrease the source capacity by the number of popped items.
    89	            // This is done at the original address; it will be copied in the next step.
    90	            brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
    91	                source_capacity.address,
    92	                item_pop_count_arg,
    93	                source_capacity.address,
    94	                BrilligBinaryOp::Sub,
    95	            );
    96	            // Re-initialize the metadata at the shifted position.
    97	            brillig_context.codegen_initialize_vector_metadata(
    98	                target_vector,
    99	                *target_size,
   100	                *source_capacity,
   101	            );
   102	        } else {
   103	            // We can't reuse the source vector, so allocate a new one.
   104	            brillig_context.codegen_initialize_vector(target_vector, *target_size, None);
   105	
   106	            let target_vector_items_pointer =
   107	                brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(target_vector);
   108	
   109	            // Set the source pointer to copy from to the source items start plus the number of popped items.
   110	            let source_copy_pointer = brillig_context.allocate_register();
   111	            brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
   112	                source_items_pointer.address,
   113	                item_pop_count_arg,
   114	                *source_copy_pointer,
   115	                BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
   116	            );
   117	            // Now we copy the source vector into the target vector, starting at index after the popped items.
   118	            brillig_context.codegen_mem_copy(
   119	                *source_copy_pointer,
   120	                *target_vector_items_pointer,
   121	                *target_size,
   122	            );
   123	            // We don't decrease the RC of the source vector, otherwise repeatedly popping the same item
   124	            // from the original (immutable) handle would bring its RC down to 1.
   125	        }
   126	    });
   127	}

   990	    /// Weave the `condition` into blackbox call arguments, returning the modified arguments.
   991	    fn handle_blackbox_side_effects(
   992	        &mut self,
   993	        condition: ValueId,
   994	        blackbox: BlackBoxFunc,
   995	        mut arguments: Vec<ValueId>,
   996	        call_stack: CallStackId,
   997	    ) -> Vec<ValueId> {
   998	        match blackbox {
   999	            BlackBoxFunc::EmbeddedCurveAdd => {
  1000	                arguments[6] = self.mul_by_condition(arguments[6], condition, call_stack);
  1001	                arguments
  1002	            }
  1003	
  1004	            BlackBoxFunc::MultiScalarMul => {
  1005	                arguments[2] = self.mul_by_condition(arguments[2], condition, call_stack);

  1007	            }

     1	use crate::ssa::{
     2	    ir::{
     3	        function::Function,
     4	        instruction::{Instruction, Intrinsic},
     5	        types::{NumericType, Type},
     6	    },
     7	    ssa_gen::Ssa,
     8	};
     9	
    10	impl Ssa {
    11	    /// A simple SSA pass to find any calls to `Intrinsic::AsSlice` and replacing any references to the length of the
    12	    /// resulting slice with the length of the array from which it was generated.
    13	    ///
    14	    /// This allows the length of a slice generated from an array to be used in locations where a constant value is
    15	    /// necessary when the value of the array is unknown.
    16	    ///
    17	    /// Note that this pass must be placed before loop unrolling to be useful.
    18	    #[expect(clippy::wrong_self_convention)]
    19	    #[tracing::instrument(level = "trace", skip(self))]
    20	    pub(crate) fn as_slice_optimization(mut self) -> Self {
    21	        for func in self.functions.values_mut() {
    22	            func.as_slice_optimization();
    23	        }
    24	        self
    25	    }
    26	}
    27	
    28	impl Function {
    29	    pub(crate) fn as_slice_optimization(&mut self) {
    30	        // If `as_slice` isn't called in this function there's nothing to do
    31	        let Some(as_slice) = self.dfg.get_intrinsic(Intrinsic::AsSlice).copied() else {
    32	            return;
    33	        };
    34	
    35	        self.simple_optimization(|context| {
    36	            let instruction_id = context.instruction_id;
    37	            let instruction = context.instruction();
    38	
    39	            let (target_func, arguments) = match &instruction {
    40	                Instruction::Call { func, arguments } => (func, arguments),
    41	                _ => return,
    42	            };
    43	
    44	            if *target_func != as_slice {
    45	                return;
    46	            }
    47	
    48	            let first_argument =
    49	                arguments.first().expect("AsSlice should always have one argument");
    50	            let array_typ = context.dfg.type_of_value(*first_argument);
    51	            let Type::Array(_, length) = array_typ else {
    52	                unreachable!("AsSlice called with non-array {}", array_typ);
    53	            };
    54	
    55	            let [original_slice_length, _] = context.dfg.instruction_result(instruction_id);
    56	            let known_length = context.dfg.make_constant(length.into(), NumericType::length_type());
    57	            context.replace_value(original_slice_length, known_length);
    58	        });
    59	    }
    60	}
    61	
    62	#[cfg(test)]
    63	mod test {
    64	    use crate::assert_ssa_snapshot;
    65	
    66	    use super::Ssa;
    67	
    68	    #[test]
    69	    fn as_slice_length_optimization() {
    70	        // In this code we expect `return v2` to be replaced with `return u32 3` because
    71	        // that's the length of the v0 array.
    72	        let src = "
    73	        acir(inline) fn main f0 {
    74	          b0(v0: [Field; 3]):
    75	            v2, v3 = call as_slice(v0) -> (u32, [Field])
    76	            return v2
    77	        }
    78	        ";
    79	        let ssa = Ssa::from_str(src).unwrap();
    80	
    81	        let ssa = ssa.as_slice_optimization();
    82	        assert_ssa_snapshot!(ssa, @r"
    83	        acir(inline) fn main f0 {
    84	          b0(v0: [Field; 3]):
    85	            v2, v3 = call as_slice(v0) -> (u32, [Field])
    86	            return u32 3
    87	        }
    88	        ");
    89	    }

    ///
    /// If the slice has zero length, this function skips the memory read and returns zero values.

    /// with "cannot pop from a slice with length 0". This prevents reading from empty memory blocks

2025-12-30 04:55:47,982 - INFO - swea-agent - 🤖 MODEL INPUT
OBSERVATION:

pub enum BrilligBinaryOp {
    Add,
    Sub,
    Mul,
    FieldDiv,
    UnsignedDiv,
    Equals,
    LessThan,
    LessThanEquals,
    And,
    Or,
    Xor,
    Shl,
    Shr,
    // Modulo operation requires more than one brillig opcode
    Modulo,
}

impl From<BrilligBinaryOp> for BinaryFieldOp {
    fn from(operation: BrilligBinaryOp) -> BinaryFieldOp {
        match operation {
            BrilligBinaryOp::Add => BinaryFieldOp::Add,
            BrilligBinaryOp::Sub => BinaryFieldOp::Sub,
            BrilligBinaryOp::Mul => BinaryFieldOp::Mul,
            BrilligBinaryOp::FieldDiv => BinaryFieldOp::Div,
            BrilligBinaryOp::UnsignedDiv => BinaryFieldOp::IntegerDiv,
            BrilligBinaryOp::Equals => BinaryFieldOp::Equals,
            BrilligBinaryOp::LessThan => BinaryFieldOp::LessThan,
            BrilligBinaryOp::LessThanEquals => BinaryFieldOp::LessThanEquals,
            _ => panic!("Unsupported operation: {operation:?} on a field"),
        }

        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
        source_vector: BrilligVector,
        removed_items: &[BrilligVariable],
    ) {
        // Check that we have enough items to pop: source_len >= pop_count
        let pop_count = self.brillig_context.make_usize_constant_instruction(removed_items.len().into());
        let has_enough_items = self.brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_mem();
        self.brillig_context.binary_instruction(
            source_len,
            *pop_count,
            *has_enough_items,
            BrilligBinaryOp::LessThanEquals,
        );
        self.brillig_context.codegen_constrain(
            *has_enough_items,
            Some("Index out of bounds".to_string()),
        );

        let read_pointer = self.brillig_context.allocate_register();
        self.brillig_context.call_vector_pop_back_procedure(
            source_len,
            source_vector,
            target_vector,
            *read_pointer,
            removed_items.len(),
        );

        self.read_variables(*read_pointer, removed_items);
    }' --new_str '    /// Create new vector with a number of (flattened) items popped from the back,
    /// then read the popped items into the variables representing the removed items.

        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,

   583	pub(crate) struct Allocated<T, R: RegisterAllocator> {
   584	    /// The inner structure is optional, so that we can map it to a different value
   585	    /// and let the original wrapper be dropped without any effect.
   586	    inner: Option<AllocatedInner<T, R>>,
   587	}
   588	
   589	/// Address list with enough slots for `HeapVector`.
   590	type AddressList = SmallVec<[MemoryAddress; 2]>;
   591	
   592	struct AllocatedInner<A, R> {
   593	    /// The value that we actually wanted to use, holding the allocated `MemoryAddress`.
   594	    value: A,
   595	    /// Addresses allocated.
   596	    addresses: AddressList,
   597	    /// Reference to the registers, for deallocation.
   598	    /// Optional so that pure values don't have to clone the registers.
   599	    registers: Option<Rc<RefCell<R>>>,
   600	}
   601	
   602	impl<A, R: RegisterAllocator> Drop for Allocated<A, R> {
   603	    fn drop(&mut self) {
   604	        let Some(mut inner) = self.inner.take() else {
   605	            return;
   606	        };
   607	        let Some(registers) = inner.registers.take() else {
   608	            return;
   609	        };
   610	        let addresses = std::mem::take(&mut inner.addresses);
   611	        let mut registers = registers.borrow_mut();
   612	        for addr in addresses {
   613	            registers.deallocate_register(addr);
   614	        }
   615	    }
   616	}
   617	
   618	/// Construct a new allocated address.
   619	impl<R: RegisterAllocator> Allocated<MemoryAddress, R> {
   620	    /// Wrap single allocated memory address.

impl<A, R: RegisterAllocator> Deref for Allocated<A, R> {
    type Target = A;

    86	    /// Read the popped number of variables from the front of the source vector,
    87	    /// then create the target vector from the source by skipping the number of popped items.
    88	    pub(crate) fn slice_pop_front_operation(
    89	        &mut self,
    90	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
    91	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    92	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    93	        removed_items: &[BrilligVariable],
    94	    ) {
    95	        // Check that we have enough items to pop: pop_count <= source_len
    96	        let pop_count = self.brillig_context.make_usize_constant_instruction(removed_items.len().into());
    97	        let has_enough_items = self.brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_mem();
    98	        self.brillig_context.binary_instruction(
    99	            *pop_count,
   100	            source_len,
   101	            *has_enough_items,
   102	            BrilligBinaryOp::LessThanEquals,
   103	        );
   104	        self.brillig_context.codegen_constrain(
   105	            *has_enough_items,
   106	            Some("Index out of bounds".to_string()),
   107	        );
   108	
   109	        let read_pointer = self.brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(source_vector);
   110	        self.read_variables(*read_pointer, removed_items);
   111	
   112	        self.brillig_context.call_vector_pop_front_procedure(
   113	            source_len,
   114	            source_vector,
   115	            target_vector,
   116	            removed_items.len(),
   117	        );
   118	    }
   119	
   120	    /// Create new vector with a number of (flattened) items popped from the back,
   121	    /// then read the popped items into the variables representing the removed items.
   122	    pub(crate) fn slice_pop_back_operation(
   123	        &mut self,
   124	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
   125	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
   126	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
   127	        removed_items: &[BrilligVariable],
   128	    ) {
   129	        // Check that we have enough items to pop: pop_count <= source_len
   130	        let pop_count = self.brillig_context.make_usize_constant_instruction(removed_items.len().into());
   131	        let has_enough_items = self.brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_mem();
   132	        self.brillig_context.binary_instruction(
   133	            *pop_count,
   134	            source_len,
   135	            *has_enough_items,
   136	            BrilligBinaryOp::LessThanEquals,
   137	        );
   138	        self.brillig_context.codegen_constrain(
   139	            *has_enough_items,
   140	            Some("Index out of bounds".to_string()),
   141	        );
   142	
   143	        let read_pointer = self.brillig_context.allocate_register();
   144	        self.brillig_context.call_vector_pop_back_procedure(
   145	            source_len,
   146	            source_vector,
   147	            target_vector,
   148	            *read_pointer,
   149	            removed_items.len(),
   150	        );
   151	
   152	        self.read_variables(*read_pointer, removed_items);
   153	    }
   154	
   155	    /// Prepare a vector for inserting a number of (flattened) items at a specific index
   156	    /// by making a hole for them, then write the variables to the returned write pointer.
   157	    pub(crate) fn slice_insert_operation(
   158	        &mut self,
   159	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
   160	        source_vector: BrilligVector,

2025-12-30 05:03:03,201 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
I notice it says:
> The `item_pop_count` equals the number of variables to pop into in SSA.
> The `source_len` is the semantic (not flattened) length of the vector.

This is important - we need to make sure we're comparing the right things. In our code:
- `source_len` is the semantic length 
- `removed_items.len()` is the number of items we're trying to pop

So we're checking: `removed_items.len() <= source_len`

This should be correct! The semantic length is what matters for the user-level bounds check.

Now let me create a comprehensive test script to help validate the fix. Let me create a simple shell script:
